RATING: 7
This is an outstanding version of 7 Wonders for two players, much better than the 2 player variant the original game provides. On every turn you are facing interesting tactical decisions which card to take and what options you leave for your opponent. This creates a similar feel to drafting cards but manages to overcome the dullness of the exercise you experience with just 2 players. Moreover, the threat of instant victory electrifies the atmosphere adding to the tension. Well done.

Perhaps this Duel version features a bit more strategic depth since you can see a part of what is coming and you can try to plan further ahead while in the original game you are navigating through foggy waters, i.e., you can try to follow some longer term plan but quite often the current draws you somewhere else.  Moreover, in addition to the wonders you can aim on the technology benefits and build your strategy on them. 

However, the game is still 7 Wonders and I would not call it better or worse as a whole. Duel is definitely an improvement for 2 players and I am happy to play it anytime.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
This game is a wonderful distillation of 7 Wonders into a 2-player game, but it's so much more than just 7 Wonders for 2.  The card pyramids are such a great way of doing drafting for two players as you have to think ahead several moves when deciding what to pick, and the face down cards create enough uncertainty to prevent players from mapping out the entire age (or feeling like they need to) for each pick.  The alternate win conditions of science and military, while uncommon, present ways for players to pressure their opponents into making moves they might not want to make, and force the players to diversify their strategies.

This game does the 7 Wonders brand justice, and is a standout in the crowded field of 2-player, head-to-head games.

RATING: 6
I really like the original 7 Wonders and this is a much better two player version than the original has. The fact that you can choose cards and no longer just draft them adds a more strategic element to the game. However, I think 7 Wonders shouldn't be a game for just two. I like the original with more players much better. From the games I played I felt that I no longer had this many ways to win as in the original. If you're unlucky in the beginning and don't manage to get the resources you need, you may have already lost. The calculation for the costs for buying resources you don't own makes it even worse in my opinion.

In short:
• better two player variant
• same great components and art as the original
• bad luck at the start and you probably lose

RATING: 6
Very similar to 7 Wonders in that your first game is kinda a lost cause, since you have no idea what works or is viable, and there are suboptimal moves that severely diminish your effectiveness if taken (but aren't obvious to a first-time player).

This is more interactive than 7 Wonders (duh).

After playing again, I think the draw has a large influence on the games, resulting in some games that feel lost the entire way and never really getting better.  If you don't get yellow cards early, or don't get resources early, you lose.  With 3 plays, it felt like there is a "best" way to play, and I don't really feel that will lead to longevity, so I do not need to own this.

RATING: 7.5
An outstanding production and a great 2-player adaptation of a modern classic in a conveniently small package. What really impressed me the most about 7 Wonders Duel is how the designers managed to create a fairly different game, which still feels a lot like the original. This is something that should really serve as a proof of their talent! 

It's almost redundant to talk about component quality. Besides maybe the cards being a little too small, everything about the production quality of this game is simply stellar! On the game-play front, 7 Wonders Duel flows perfectly fast and smooth thanks to the mechanism of the pyramid. This elegant solution keeps the game simple, preserves the drafting-feel but it also creates a tense back-and-forth between the players. The overall experience is indeed significantly tighter than regular 7 Wonders. The game really got much meaner... it's a real duel, where you're messing up with your opponent all the time by denying him/her cards, developing a monopoly of one resource or menacing him/her with military strength.

All that being said, I still prefer regular 7 Wonders because of the expansions that it got, which significantly enhance the game-play for me by adding variety, depth and interesting combos. Duel doesn't offer yet quite as much of that... but I think the expansion will fix this issue very soon. I do have instead a minor complaint about the game. Because of how the pyramid works, it's terribly important to manipulate the turn order... and therefore it's really crucial to get the wonders that allow you to take another turn. Otherwise you might find yourself in a position where there's no way you can deny your opponent the card that he/she really needs. This creates a weird feeling of unbalanced first-player problem... which is actually not entirely there, because you just need to learn how to address it.

It still used to bother me a little though before Pantheon came along. The expansion in fact pretty much solves the problem by giving you the possibility of buying God Cards on your turn instead of taking a card from the pyramid. If used well, this new mechanism can prevent your opponent from taking that one card he/she needs. At the same time, Pantheon also introduced a new layer of strategy and tactics, that spiced up the game-play quite a bit, making it therefore a better experience.

Overall 7 Wonders Duel is a very well put together package. It's easy to carry around, it has beautiful artwork and components and it offers a pretty interesting game-play. It can be mean, but it's a great game for couples that don't mind a little confrontation every now and then. Recommended!

Rating without the expansion: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
FAVOURITE GAME -this is very good 2 player variant for 7 Wonders. It keeps the original "city building" feeling but the mechanics are quite different from the original game. Instead of drafting you have pre-defined laying patterns for each age, also the trading mechanism is a bit hardened as you have to be aware of what your opponent is collecting, because your trading cost will depend on them. Also it is interresting that you now have three victory conditions: by getting the most points at the end or you may win by military (getting a lot of red cards) or by science (getting a lot of green cards). I would say it is one of the best two-player games on the market.

RATING: 6
1st play: This captures a lot of the feel of 7 wonders, and I like the idea that it's possible to win with science or military now.  The game is fast, and the draft is clever.  I'm not a huge fan of 7 wonders, I'm always willing to play tho, and this is a suitable replacement for 7 wonders when there's only 2 players.  Because almost every card comes out every game, I don't know how similar repeat plays will feel.

2nd play: The game is fine, true to the original 7 wonders.  I'm not a huge fan of 7 wonders, though I won't turn down a game.  I've never felt the need to own it and this implementation feels the same to me.  The problem is, one of the strengths of 7 wonders is the flexibility of player counts.  Duel gives that up.  Plenty of 2p games I'd rather play.

RATING: 8
I enjoyed 7 wonders very much when it was released, but I played it so much and got over it for quite a while. The two first expansions are great and I think the game is not playable without them anymore, and I got enough of 7 wonders already.

7 Wonders: Duel has a lot of good ideas from new abilities of the leader and cities expansions mixed into a new implementation focused only in 2 player game. And guys, it worked so well. Bruno Cathala surely was a good addiction to the design team and now we have another great game for 2 players. Let's remember that the original 7 Wonders have a variant for 2 players, but it is not even comparable to this new experience.

Now we have the military strength excess work a role in the game and the science plays a little bit different in a way that it simply can win the game or put new strategies and possibilities for the player.

This new version is very amazing and surprised me in a positive way.

RATING: 8.9
My wife and I love to play 2 player strategy games.  Many times a week, we will sit down to play.  Since we bought this game about 3 months ago, it has become the first thing we grab.  We have had to print off more scoring sheets (we keep track of every game).  I don't think we've ever played less than 3 times in a sitting.  Every game is different.  We are always trying new things to develop new strategies.  And what is crazy is that we always have these moments when the cards are just not being revealed in our favor, and one of of is getting irate, yet we are still able to pull off a victory.  The 3 different methods of winning are key to the replayability of this game.  All you have to do is pretend to be going for a military or science victory to get your opponent nervous.  If they don't get nervous and change up the play-style, keep going, you might actually secure a military or science victory.  If you wait too long to take  a military victory seriously, it can become your sole purpose to keep military cards out of the other person's hand.  That frees up the other person to just rack up the additional points.  There are also lots of sneaky ways to accomplish your goals.

The only problem I have with it is that it is not possible to gain a science token on the 1st age, but at least half of the science tokens are really only useful if your get them early.  There might be creative ways of using them, but many of them NEVER get bought because they are NEVER useful by the time they are available.  I wish the science cards were more randomized throughout the game. Also, you might go for science early, not knowing if there will even be a possible science victory in the third age, with the way the cards are randomized.  It would be nice to know that there is at lease some way to gain a science victory in every game.

RATING: 5
I got to be honest here... This game relies upon a lot of symbol recognition...
Having played 7 Wonders before... this still presents a challenge... not helped by the ~5mm symbols utilised upon the small cards.
Some larger cards or larger symbols upon the cards would definitely be good in any future reprints; although would have an impact upon table space.
Even having played 7 Wonders previously; we felt more than a bit lost in our first couple of games... significant symbol recognition is required...
We find the rules a little vague; lacking clarity in some parts; again not helped by the significance of symbols furthermore the quantity of them.
I like the game, don't get me wrong on that... but there are definitely better duelling games out there...
Playing on similar table size & cost; Lost Cities; Star Realms; Fungi; Tiny Epic Galaxies; and on a similar city building theme I'd recommend San Juan over this.

RATING: 7
It's 7 Wonders for two players with some nice design tweaks.  After a zillion plays of the parent game, I still fail to calculate science card sets correctly,  so their simplification is welcome.  So too is the tug of war of military power; no longer can a civilization ignore its own defence entirely.  The drafting from card pyramids also works quite well.  The elevation of trade cards  through the boost they give to your income is good too.  However, in my final analysis, none of these things make Duel a better game for two than its daddy is for higher numbers.  Therefore it gets the same rating from me.

The artwork is OK and the iconography is clear.  Production quality seems to have taken a slight dip; as well as being smaller, the cards feel quite thin.

RATING: 8
Καινούργια έκδοση του δημοφιλούς 7 wonders σχεδιασμένη για 2 άτομα. Θα παραδεχθώ πως δεν δοκίμασα ποτέ την 2 player εκδοχή του βασικού 7 wonders γιατί έπαιζε χρησιμοποιώντας dummy player. Εδώ όμως τα πράματα είναι διαφορετικά. Οι κάρτες της κάθε εποχής ξεκινούν κάτω στο τραπέζι και οι παίκτες επιλέγουν με την σειρά ποια θέλουν να πάρουν. Είναι τοποθετημένες σε πυραμίδα και όπως τις παίρνουμε ανοίγουν σιγά σιγά οι επόμενες. :)  

Κατά τα άλλα υπάρχουν μικρές διαφορές στο πως λειτουργεί το market αφού πλέον πληρώνεις στην τράπεζα για να αγοράσεις υλικά ενώ οι πράσινες τεχνολογικές κάρτες είτε σου δίνουν απευθείας νίκη αν μαζέψεις 6 διαφορετικές είτε σου δίνουν μεγάλα μπόνους αν μαζέψεις 2 ίδια. 

Ωραία και η αλλαγή στο military σκέλος του παιχνιδιού. Λειτουργεί σαν διελκυστίνδα και αναγκάζεις τον αντίπαλο να χάσει χρήματα όσο τον πιέζεις ενώ μπορείς να φτάσεις σε άμεση νίκη αν το τερματίσεις.:arrrh:

O κάθε παίκτης ξεκινά με 4 θαύματα που μπορεί να χτίσει το καθένα με διαφορετικά μπόνους. Ωραία πινελιά είναι το γεγονός πως μόνο τα 7 από αυτά θα μπορέσουν να χτιστούν, οπότε υπάρχει και εκεί μια σχετική αγωνία για το αν θα προλάβεις να χτίσεις τα δικά σου 4. 

Το artwork είναι εξαιρετικό όμως οι κάρτες είναι μικρού μεγέθους. Αυτό βέβαια έχει και τα καλά του γιατί μεταφέρετε πιο εύκολα και παίζεται και σε τραπεζάκι καφετέριας. 

Μια πολύ καλή επιλογή για 2 άτομα. Ευχάριστο παιχνίδι με λογική διάρκεια γύρω στα 20 λεπτά, και μπόλικες επιλογές. Πολύ καλά σχεδιασμένο. Well done! :)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
With Pantheon expansion.

The pinnacle of boardgame 'gamefeel': everything one does feels substantial and consequential *immediately*. This system-feedback is clearest in high-tension games with very simple mechanics, where one does very little on their turn, and capitalizes on the required transparency of boardgames (i.e., that all the ways to modify the game state, and exactly how they work and respond, have to be known by the players to run the rules of the game). It's most satisfying in games with minimal luck where you KNOW you can take paths a, b and c, and what the result of each will be, and can do it in a minute of thought. There needs to be a very short space between what you do and the consequences of that action. "I take a card, I immediately let you take that other one I wanted to build your wonder and take another turn, netting that other one you wanted" feels very different than "I perform the most stastically favourable actions that have no short (and sometimes no predictable long) term consequences". 

Mechanical, yes, but system-poetry. While playing I actually appreciate the design so much it interferes with me PLAYING it; not ideal.

Much of this is diluted by the expansion, however, though it has many virtues of its own.

RATING: 6
I found this game to be a major disappointment. For me, the original 7 Wonders was/is quite a fun game with rhythmic "group activity" card passing and drafting, quirky player interactions wherein you buy resources from and "attack" neighboring players with military cards, experience the thrill of finally completing your wonder, and sorting through seemingly brilliantly compiled and thoroughly play-tested card sets. What a design!

By contrast, this game had none of this magic for me.  No passing.  No drafting.  Boring tug of war style attacking. Single stage wonders, and card sets that didn't seem to flow very smoothly.  For my tastes, this was an average resource gathering and conversion card game based upon three sets of cards arranged in pyramids, a mechanic which felt curiously mediocre to me.  Where is the magical feeling in any of this?

This game, for my tastes, does not stand very tall on its own merits, but instead, gains its evident following from gamers who are absolutely fanatical about anything related to 7 Wonders.  Yes, but if this game were to have been released before the original 7 Wonders, would this game be considered great on its own merits?  Simply put, is this a GREAT game?  Or, is this merely a good game? For me, this plays and feels very average. There are many far better two player games out there.

RATING: 2
The core game has an unacceptable flaw: Tiles MUST be picked by both players, meaning the highest priority tile will be decided if it is reached in an odd or in an even number of picks. Red and Green ones make you automatically win, so if one player is able to access there tiles uncontested, they will win. If you center your strategy around one of those, it is a matter of luck if you get them or not.

The expansion solves this, but the base game, because of this fault, gets a 2/10 from me.

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
This is 7 Wonders as the two player game we truly hoped it would be. It puts the two-player variant in 7 Wonders to shame. Instead of tradition drafting you take cards from a display between the players. Some cards are free (whether just costing nothing or perhaps having an icon that one of your cards in your tableau already has) or cost some resources that you will need to have built up before hand. But the display is set up so that as cards are taken, cards that were inaccessible become available. So it is a good give and take with you wanting the card in the display but seeing that taking it will allow your opponent to take a card that will help them. And the alternate victory conditions (getting enough military to decimate your opponent's civilization or getting enough science to make your civilization superior) make that card drafting from the display even more critical. You may want to take that science card that gets you closer to your victory but that will uncover a military card that will allow your foe to advance and make it even worse for you. Balanced perfectly, 7 Wonders Duel is one of the best two-player games on the market.

RATING: 9
Bought this last year, played 2 games with a beer friend and we both REALLY liked it.  Vowed to play more of it, but between our game group growing (meaning less 2 player games) and other new stuff, this went on the shelf.  Well, went to game night last night and only one other person showed.  Happened to have this in my bag, just in case.  We broke it out and re-familiarized ourselves with the rules.  Played through and WOW, what a great game.  Why have I not played this sooner?  Even though the other player took control of resources, blue cards and coin generation.  I had a lock on the reserves, so I could buy what I wanted.  Any my military was monster.  So, by the third age, as my opponent started taking over science, it really was the showdown of an enlighted, huge thriving city versus the small import-only military complex.  It came down to the last face down card draw in age three.  Two cards, me one space away from military victory, even though I was the clear loser in every other facet.  50/50 shot, I choose and flip the card....  and it's a blue card.  OUCH!  Final score, 74 to 48.  I got trounced, but loved every minute of the matchup.  That, my friend, is a great game.  Get it.

Update, liked this game so much, I went and got the Broken Token organizer for this one.  It has become the latest go-to for my girlfriend and I.  We are really enjoying it.

RATING: 7
It takes the theme and feel of the original with a new card drafting system. I like the science and military victory conditions that add other paths to victory. There's a lot of tough decisions that need to be made, trying to get what you need while not setting up your opponent.

One major problem is that the game can feel very scripted. There are points in the game where you can map out the next five or so moves: If I take this, then you take that, which means I'll take this, etc.

There can also be a lot of uncontrollable luck based on how the cards are laid out. Sometimes, a specific resource card is out of reach or not included in the game at all, which can just ruin one of the players.

RATING: 7.5
Initial rating, based on playing once. Has a lot of the feel from the original 7 Wonders, while still very much being its own game. The main difference is that you frequently know exactly what benefit your opponent will get if you take a specific card, which influences tactics a lot. And that makes the luck of the draw worse for the unknown cards, particularly when either player is close to a sudden death military or scientific victory, which the newly revealed card potentially ending the game. I suspect I'd get thoroughly annoyed by that aspect after a couple more plays, and would reduce the rating because of it.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Honestly, didn't have high expectations for this game. Like other "2-player adaptations of x game," I thought this game would either feel uninspiring (too similar) to its predecessor or dull, as it fails to capture everything fun about its predecessor. But this game manages to be original/unique while preserving the fair/fun of 7-wonders. 

Essentially, the game is a race... and there are a lot of races going on simultaneous. Players need to worry about the military and science conditions, as they can end the game early, but they also need to be cognitive about the wonders (only 7 can be built) and double science tokens (they give players very powerful progress tokens). Mechanically, the race is achieved through card-drafting, which is done in a way that creates replayability without too much randomness (half the cards are shown, all but 3 cards of each age will come out, etc). And even if an opponent manages to get "lucky" and pull off a win, the game plays so quick that you can play best-of-x.

Overall, there is a lot of think about and the game manages to play quickly. I like it quite a bit.

There are multiple paths to victory and you have to pay particular attention to what your opponent is focusing on at all times. The card drafting mechanism is interesting in that you may not want to take your best option as it will open up opportunities for your opponent. Overall, I think this game holds alot of promise for repeated plays and I'm looking forward to delving into it.

RATING: N/A
(2 Players, 30 min, CLASSIC) A 2-player version of 7 Wonders, in which players build a civilization by drafting resources, buildings, and technologies from a deck of shuffled cards laid out in an overlapping pyramid. Every choice exposes more cards for your opponent to draft, so what you choose is as important as what you give away!

RATING: 8.5
Excellent 1 v 1 mini-civilization builder that actually plays within the advertised time range - a 30 minute game that actually feels satisfying! Definitely my favorite game for when we (my wife and I) are short on time (week nights) - and will play it even if we do have extra time. Lots of fun with multiple strategies and win conditions (military, science or victory points / infrastructure - of which you have a couple different ways you can accrue the needed resources) - has some 'take that' player interaction via wonders, which is awesome, and games often come down to the last couple of turns which provides a satisfying level of tension. 

*** Great game to play with my 9 year old son, he picked it up on his first play through.

RATING: 8.5
Impressed out of the gate by this arguable "spin-off" of a game. All that is true about 7 Wonders is here (the choice between keeping something you want or keeping your opponent from a card they need, science and combat being important, and the construction of wonders)- but each are presented in a fresh, interesting way. Drafting is from a structure "mah-jongg" style, military and science can win you the game immediately if unchecked, and you receive several wonders instead of one. Fascinating...may be rated higher after more plays!

RATING: 7.5
I like 7 wonders but something's bugging me in this game. I guess it's a nice variant of 7 wonders for two players, but it's not as good as the original.

I don't like that there are frequently situations in which you are forced to pick a certain card; in 7 wonders there are at least two cards you can choose from.

At the beginning of the third age, I could see that I was bound to lose: My opponent was collecting the green cards and missing one symbol. Unfortunately, the missing symbol was on both of the cards in the last row (the row that was dealt first). And since there was no possibility for me to take both of the two last cards, I lost on the final card.

RATING: 8
Duel takes the very few passable bits of Seven Wonders (like building the eponymous wonders), works on them and delivers a surprisingly good two-player game that both holds the flavor of the original and at the same time improves on it: the real wonder here is how this lighter version turns the original dull multiplayer solitaire into such a fun game with lots of interactions.
Just for doing this, it should be dubbed "the eighth wonder". [i](May 2016)[/i]

[b]Update[/b] - I’ve been playing Duel several times now and I’ve enjoyed every single game so far.
Sure, the strategy is quite straightforward and doesn’t evolve too much from game to game, nonetheless it still does its job just fine: that is, the job of  a short, light game for two that requires a little improvisation and doesn’t burn your brain.
Thus, in October 2017 I raised my rating from 7 to 8.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Now this is what a 7 Wonders two player game should be. Despite the arguments of some on the site who defended the original game's two player variant, I was always dissatisfied with it. 7 Wonders: Duel creates a clever tiled setup which creates an even greater drafting mechanism than that of the original in my opinion. The tug of war on the military track fits perfectly as well as the threat of superior scientific advancement. It has much more of a take-that element which balances out the risk of the game becoming just a thinky, multi-step math chaining operation. It has a small footprint of rules with a good dose of interesting decisions. There is some luck of the draw as two players playing well can win or lose based on what card happens to be face down on the card setup. Regardless, this is a winner. I actually like it more than the original 7 Wonders. I rate it an 8 at present with a good chance of it becoming a 9 on future plays.

RATING: 8.75
Decent setup time, quick to play, interactive, strategic and tactical. A good 2 player game, that misses the excitement of surprise plays, bluffing or game-changing plays and instead focuses on balanced play with only some hidden information. Every careful decision only brings you a small step towards victory and thus this game is rather slow paced and strategic at its core, while it still manages to flow quickly and never leaves a player out of options.

Overall very good quick 2 player game.

RATING: 10
Duel might be the best filler I've played - it certainly is the only filler to crack my personal top 10. Within its relatively short playing time is contained more tension than in many games thrice its length. Why? It's a tooth and nail battle across multiple fronts: build the greatest civ and win on VPs, OR defeat your opponent for an instant win with military might, OR outpace your opponent on the technological front for a different instant win.

With three win conditions to track and keep in balance, the game offers myriad tactical opportunities. The mechanics only amplify and augment the tension and decisions. At the forefront is the unique card tableau from which choices are made. By making only some cards visible, forward planning is possible, but only partially, and those hidden cards not only hide opportunity, but anxiety as well. Many a game is lost, for example, by flopping over a pair of cards at the end of your turn revealing a hidden military card that puts your opponent over the top. Thus tactics often shift towards not wanting to reveal new cards - a delicious tension develops between wanting to see what is hidden but wanting to force your opponent to make the reveal, even at the cost of taking a less than optimal card. 

And because this is a zero sum battle, you can calculate with some precision exactly who will (or at least can) attain which card, making the psychological dimension of the game deep, as you attempt to intuit, and at times lead, your opponent's thinking. Thus the rarity of the double turn, the only way to trump such determinancies, adds greatly to the tension and provides a pivot for the competition.

I still have not done justice to how much fun this battle of wills is, all the result of an incredibly lucid, elegant design. One of the great 2 player games.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
It's a nice strategy game for 2, up with Agricola: All Creatures Big and Small and Le Havre: The Inland Port. It's pretty good, but I do feel like the strategy of the game will wear off as there are few 'unseen' parts of the game: pretty much everything is on the table and given that it's you vs them, you'll have had everything at one point or other.

RATING: 7

The best part about this game is that it's drafting that doesn't require memory, which is a great improvement to 7 Wonders (the memory aspect of drafting games is my least favorite part about them).

:thumbsup: [b]POSITIVE POINTS:[/b]

++ A great implementation of 7 Wonders for 2 players only (my most common player count), that capture most of the feel of the original game, but with new gameplay, now with more tension and in a small package.
++ I like the new way of drafting, using an imperfect information method, showing only half the cards and also removing 3 cards per Age per game. This add to the tension, when you draft a card that will reveal new cards to your opponent, but also when you are trying to shape your strategy (ex. Are there a lot of military cards or Science cards that are out of the games?).
++ I really like the alternative way of winning, the science victory and the great implementation of the military conflict that work great and that really show the duel. This add a layer of putting pressure on your opponent, forcing them to pay attention to their opponent.
++ I like that science is no longer just a set collection, and that you can get Progress token which may help your strategy, which add another new layer to the game.
++ Great game insert which hold everything in an orderly fashion (though, as usual, I will need to get rid of it to fit in the expansion).
++ Great card graphic design, that is clean and clear (better than the original which was already great).
++ Easy to teach (super easy to teach if you have played 7 Wonders before, as you will be familiar with most of the iconography), fast to set-up and fast to play.
++ There is one expansion available for this game (which is useful to refresh the game when we have overplayed it).
++ Adding in Pantheon increase the gameplay depth and lower the randomness by adding a new twist to the game, without too much new rules.
++ Adding in Pantheon really multiple the possibilities of strategy (and refine the obvious one, like the scientific victory is now easier to achieve) and also correct the problem of a player being screwed at the beginning of Age 3, because by invoking the god power, you no longer have to take a cards from the pyramid, and thus you can change the order of the draw this way too.
++ A second expansion is in the work.

 

:thumbsdown: [b]NEGATIVE POINTS:[/b]

-- I'm was not really fond of the way the ressources cost, scaling the value according to the number of this same ressource produce by your opponent. My wife found it fiddly to always having to check my tableau to calculate the cost of her ressources and sometimes miscalculated (after a few games this no longer happens though, so now, I guess this is no longer a negative, as this method is good because it's another way to put pressure on your opponent).
-- Component wise, everything was of good quality, but my Wonder cards where really warped. The replacements sent were also warped (which is a bummer when you ask for replacement cards and you receive warped cards again). After a month under more than 50 pounds of book over them, they are now still a bit curved but playable, but they still tend to curve back over time.
-- It's a 2-players only game, and for whatever reason, I don't like buying 2-players only games, even though I play a lot of my game just with my wife.
-- Sometime, either if you opponent doesn't play well, or because of the really unfortunate cards order, one player can be pretty much screwed at the beginning of the 3rd age, knowing he/she has already lost and this is not fun for that player (but this is really rare (1 game out of 15 maybe), as usually, even if you think you lag behind or you are maybe screwed, there are ways to change that).
-- Adding in Pantheon increase a lot the downtime in some games (because it add so much possibilities), lengthen the setup time a bit and lengthen the game time (but not too much to be detrimental).

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A really nice two-player game, taking many mechanisms and ideas from 7 wonders, and reshaping them to make it more interesting for two.

The two big changes are:

1) Instead of drafting, a pyramid of cards is created, and players may only choose cards that aren't stuck under other cards of the pyramid. This creates an interesting dynamic of getting cards you want, but being wary of "unlocking" useful cards for your opponent.

2) Instant win conditions. Military has been converted to a tug-of-war type battle, where each military you play pushes a military token toward your opponent's side of the military track. If you get the token all the way down the track you win. Science has also turned into an instant win for collecting a large variety of science cards. This also adds a lot of interest, as you need to watch out for what you allow your opponent to take for fear of them advancing to an instant win.

Overall, a really nice game, rather than the cash grabs you often see on these spin-offs of popular titles.

RATING: 8
I've only played it twice. It's much better than two player 7 Wonders and I think it might be a better game overall. It basically 'feels' the same as regular 7 Wonders, but the small difference add up to a very different gaming experience.  

I'm a little concerned about how overpowered a lucky resource distribution appears to be, but more plays will tell whether bad luck can be overcome with skill. If not, the game is still good, but I could see it finally being closer to a six or seven. Better-luck-next-time is not the sort of thing I'm looking for in a game of this type. 

Still, it has a little bit more to think about than the multiplayer version and it seems like there might be several different ways to win, especially with the auto-win possibilities in military and progress. I also really like the drafting board, which gives the game a nice combination of look-ahead and randomness. 

Time will tell. I will revisit these comments as I play more.

RATING: 9
[b]Includes 7 Wonders Duel: Pantheon[/b]

I'm glad I read reviews on this one. I would have never guessed that this is a game I'd want to own based on my lackluster interest in the original. It's a very different game compared to standard 7 Wonders. The symbols all look the same, but the drafting of cards from the various pyramid shapes each round adds a totally new dimension very suitable for two players.

I think this is a game that both my wife and I will enjoy, very much up there with other classic two-player-only games like Battle Line and such.

Update: four plays now, and I can safely say this might be one of the best two-player games that is playable in 45 minutes. The three possible win conditions of military, science, or points adds a surprising amount of tension. There's a heck of a lot of game in this little box, and it's become a favorite of one of my coworkers.

RATING: 6
What I like about the game is that it looks gorgeous. Somebody went the extra mile here. I also enjoy the variety of strategies that are offered. Three different ways to win the game, that's unique!

A negative point would be the tiny cards. I like to build things, to create cities, to dwell in the majesty of my creation, to intimidate my opponent, but building these micro-civilisations is neither satisfying nor intimidating.  

Another thing that bothers me are the guild cards. I don't really find them interesting. Sure, you can get a lot of points from them, but they are somehow out of place in the third age. It's the game's grand finale and what do you do? You count cards. It slows down the game and takes away a lot of the suspense. 

In general, there is too much going on for me for such a "small" game, and I have a hard time looking at the many different symbols, comparing my opponent's cards with my own etc.  

One last thing: this game is mean on a very uncomfortable level. I have no problems with open confrontation, like in Chess or Magic: The Gathering. When you play these games, you know what you get. But every time I directly hurt my opponent in 7 Wonders: Duel, it just feels mean to me, because i could have done something else instead. For example, I could have picked up something else than the military card that makes my opponent lose money; I could have activated another wonder instead of the one that destroys a building which my opponent desperately needs. It feels like I have the choice: to live in peaceful harmony with my opponent, play my little solo game and focus on making my city great and prosperous; but instead, just because I am mean bastard, I make my opponent suffer. Not enough to make it appear like a declaration of war. Just sporadically, just enough to get on my opponent's nerves.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Wow, 7 Wonders Duel comes in a small box but packs a powerful punch.  With just two players every decision seems crucial.  It feels like there is so much going on each round and money becomes real tight if you aren't careful.  Of the games I have played this and The Voyages of Marco Polo are my favourite of 2015.

RATING: 5
First impression: Neat transcription of the full game into a 2 player-version. The authors have gotten rid of some cruft, and worked hard to make it all work for both opponents. I'm strongly inclined to say that they succeeded quite well. The advantage is that it will all make you feel right at home... but the disadvantage is the very strong zero-sum nature of the game, and difficulty in selecting a proper upgrade path of your own because of how half the cards in an era is placed face down. Therefore you're limited by what is available, and have to make do with simplistic [i]If I don't take that card then she will and that will prove a greater threat so I have to bury it[/i]-deliberations. I've long since outgrown such niceties, but for others it might just strike the right chord. Still, there's not a great deal in the ways of strategy available to you: it's military, blue buildings, yaddayaddayadda. (Told you you'd feel right at home.)

It was genuinely nice to have played the game, but I think the buck stops here.

RATING: 8
Great adaptation of the 7 Wonders mechanics for two players. The game feels very much like it's big sibling, while being much tighter and more enjoyable than the original 2-player workaround. After several plays, there doesn't seem to be a dominant strategy, but rather a dynamic back and forth between both players competing for cards, resources and military might. RATING: 8.4
As anyone who's tried it knows, the 2-player variant for 7 Wonders never worked well. Anyone I know abandoned it in favor of other options like playing multiple boards at once. So a true 2-player reimplementation was welcome!

This will feel very familiar to those who have played 7W, with a few key differences. For example, the cost to purchase resources from a neighbor is not fixed, military power is a constant push-pull, and science is now a strategy you really have to commit to in order to make it work. These changes were easy to grasp so veterans can just about dive right in.

I would like to play this more to get a feel for how much depth and replayability it has. But in general I'm feeling favorable towards this being a two-player option we'll reach for regularly.

RATING: 10
This game provides a lot for a tiny box it has. It is designed to be a battle between 2 players only and I believe it really shines in what it do.
There is a huge amount of tactics in which card to pick (not only what I need, but also pick what my opponent desperately needs). There are three ways of victory (points, science, military) so you can play strategically but I believe you should focus on what is best for you now.

What I like:
- Interesting and original drafting mechanism (different card pyramids for each of the three ages)
- Very quick play time (my experience is between 20-25 minutes per game), yet the games are very intense.
- tiny box, and the content could be in even smaller box, so great when traveling for example. Therefore I like the small cards. I don't have any issue with them at all.
- I must repeat myself, but I am amazed how much the game provides for just a small content. Simple and easy grasped rules, tight game play, interesting decisions.

What I dislike:
- Although civilization theme, I don't care about the card meaning. I don't build Sawmill, I just build 2wood resource for 2 gold. The pictures on cards are tiny and I really don't care about them as well. Theme is a mediocre at best.
- This game could be unforgiving and harsh. In case one of players is much better than another, the game could be frustrating for the other one.
- My only game wise con is that Wonders with the extra round ability are too strong and they are first pick material no matter what. There is simply no way to leave this wonder and pick the one without extra round, which I found annoying a bit.

RATING: 8.5
I already liked the 2 player variant of the original 7 Wonders, but this is even better.
I think the main reason I consider it to be an excellent game is that is has three different paths to victory (civilian, military, and scientific) and all three kinds of victory can realistically be achieved. This helps a lot to keep the game suspenseful until shortly before its end. One player may have a large lead in victory points, but because he probably neglected military and/or science in order to get his VP, the other player often still has a good chance to win the game.
Moreover, I like how the designers managed to create quite a deep game with such a short playing time.
It is also nice that it is so small and thus easily transportable.

RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
As a companion to 7 Wonders, this offers just enough of a unique take that I'm happy to have it in my collection. My girlfriend loves playing it, though neither of us has much of a handle on the strategy after five or six games. We've already had her win a game through military might, and me win a science game, even though both seem highly unlikely in the grand scheme of things. 

Biggest dislike is the cards themselves, which are very small and slippery and kind of unpleasant to handle. Beyond that, the mechanics of the game are solid, though jumping over from normal 7 Wonders requires a bit of adapting. In regular 7 Wonders trashing cards is a part of a specific sort of strategy, but not something you do all that often. In my limited experience with 7WD, you end up trashing a fair number of cards, which means that early Yellow cards are a huge boon to your coin revenue and thus your mid- and late-game plotting. If you fall way behind on Yellows it can be tough to get back into the game.

Strongest positives are the cool pyramids that you get to make with the cards that add a wrinkle to a 2P drafting game. As you get more experienced, you learn what the risks and rewards of opening up a certain facedown card might be, and you can mindgame your opponent into thinking you want to pursue one strategy rather than another. On the other hand, because there is perfect information about your opponent's cards, you should never feel TOO blindsided by a particular event. The way Wonders work in this game is also pretty cool, and deciding whether or not to prioritize a Wonder strategy early is a lot different than in the normal game.

This game is one of our current favorites for a quick option after dinner/before bed.

Beer Comparison: a well-made, consistently enjoyable Brown Ale like Bell's.

Vous connaissez 7Wonders ? Le jeu qui a gagné tous les prix ludiques possibles et inimaginables il y a quelques années ? Si vous ne connaissez pas, on ne peut que vous encourager à le découvrir. Ou alors découvrir 7Wonders Duel, qui est sa variante à 2 joueurs. Alors, ne me faites pas dire ce que j'ai pas dit : ce n'est pas le même jeu ! Même thématique, même graphisme, sensations de jeu assez proches, mais la mécanique change tout de même avec un système de cartes pyramidale que l'on va prendre à tour de rôle, toujours pour produire des ressources avec des cartes marrons, construire nos bâtiments améliorés avec les cartes jaunes, s'améliorer en militaire avec les cartes rouges, faire du prestige avec les cartes bleu, etc ... Proche de 7Wonders, mais pas 7Wonders. Un peu partout, j'entends dire que c'est le meilleur des jeux à 2 (du moment, ça c'est sur, mais rien ne détrônera Caribooh )

Pour 2 joueurs, pour des parties de 25 minutes environ

RATING: 6.9
Maybe i´m being too harsh here, but the general feeling after just one play is disappointment, taking into account  its "father" game.
There is no need to search for materials as anything you don´t have may be bought to the bank (commerce cards just saves you one coin), military power is almost irrelevant since it´s easy to keep the balance in a plain "thug of war" line, science advantage is almost null unless you gather six cards but this is easily prevented by your oppponent, etc. Also odd, is the fact of beeing normal the last few cards serves you no purpose and need to be discarded for coins. 
Furthermore, i feel this is a game that makes little sense out of its own, i mean, for people who don´t know 7 wonders and don´t feel the need for a two player version of the game, this looks like a quite weak game.
At least, the nice artwork and the swift mechanics of the original game are still present here, not so bad.

RATING: 7.2
7 Wonders Duel is a nice 2 player game, and a good variant on the ever so popular 7 Wonders.

I like the alternative win conditions (though they are more a way to force the opponent to react than to actually win), the very nice inlay and how quick it is played. What I like less is the fiddly and small cards (though that might be my problem) and what I do not like is that after 8-10 games it seems more and more that randomness is a VERY big factor in this game. Who begins is very relevant, what cards you uncover is VERY relevant (to the point where your opponent just loses if you have eg 1-2 Wonders that let you have another turn and you can 'steal' all the science cards your opponent can't reach in time), but all in all a good game. 

This is how you pack a smallbox game correctly, splendor/NMBR9!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
2

Voorbereiding :

-	Rood schild in het midden van het bord
-	4 militaire tokens open op het bord
-	5 wetenschapstokens op het bord
-	Elke speler krijgt 7 geld
-	Selectie van de wonders: er liggen 4 willekeurige wonders, de eerste speler kiest een wonder, de tweede speler kiest twee wonders en tenslotte neemt de eerste speler het overgebleven wonder. Doe dit nogmaals, maar laat nu de tweede speler beginnen met kiezen.
-	Verwijder 3 kaarten uit elke tijdperk stapel, voeg 3 paarse kaarten toe aan de tijdperk 3stapel. Verwijder de overige paarse kaarten.

Handelen:

-	Je kan altijd ontbrekende grondstoffen van de bank kopen.
-	Kost = 2 + aantal symbolen van dezelfde grondstof (bruin en grijs) bij de tegenspeler
-	Sommige gele kaarten zorgen ervoor dat je voor een grondstof slechts 1 munt moet betalen.

Speeloverzicht:

Leg de kaarten zoals aangeduid op het voorbeeld.
Kies een kaart die vrij ligt (niet afgedekt door 1 of 2 andere kaarten).

1/ betaal de kost en bouw de kaart
2/ leg de kaart op de aflegstapel en ontvang 2 geld (+1 geld voor elke gele kaart in je stad)
3/ bouw een wonder

Als het zevende wonder is gebouwd, verdwijnt het achtste wonder uit het spel.

De speler die het er slechtst voor staat op militair gebied, kiest wie het volgende tijdperk mag beginnen.

Militair: voor elk schild verplaats je het schild een vakje dichter naar de zone van de tegenspeler. Als het schild het laatste vakje van de tegenspeler bereikt, win je onmiddellijk.

Wetenschap: elke keer als je twee groene kaarten met hetzelfde symbool verzamelt, mag je onmiddellijk een wetenschapstoken nemen. Wanneer je 6 verschillende symbolen hebt verzameld, win je het spel onmiddellijk.

Wanneer niemand wint via wetenschap of door het militaire gevecht, dan wint de speler met het meeste overwinningspunten.

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
A quick playing, dedicated two player game, adapted from the 7 Wonders universe.  Gone is the Fairly Tale pass the cards mechanic, replaced by alternately drawing cards off a pyramid structure in the centre of the table.  As cards are drawn, other cards are unlocked and/or revealed, possibly giving opportunities to your opponent.  A tug of war military track replaces the war with neighbours mechanic from the original game.  The rest feels nice and familiar.  Three spheres of victory means you have to watch your opponent carefully and react accordingly. 

First game was good, second game was "hmmm, is that it?".  It felt too easy, with no tension.  The bloom will fall from this rose quite quickly I suspect.  Much, much better two player games on the shelf for this to compete with - not a good sign.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
7 Wonders: Duel is the attempt to make 7 Wonders into a better game than the 2-player variant included with the main game. As with most people, I definitely see this as a success. In fact, I like it a lot more than 7 Wonders. The main reason for this, is that it keeps the basics of 7 Wonders (drafting, resources, military, science, guilds, unique wonders, etc.) but amps up the tension of the game. How does it do this? 

-Instead of Science and Millitary just being VP paths in 7WD, they can instantly end the game in victory for the person that focuses on it. 

-The pool drafting of where there are some cards face-down and some face-up (and how these are flipped up) can be really nerve wracking. Especially when opponents are going for Military/Science victory.

-Resource management is even trickier since resources opponents acquire make your deficiencies in those specific resources, more expensive to deal with.

-Each player starts with 4 wonders each. That said, the game is called 7 Wonders for a reason... As soon as a player builds their fourth Wonder, that denies their opponent from  ever building their fourth.

The replay value of this game is fairly decent. You don't use all of the science progress markers, guilds or wonders each game. There are also 3 cards randomly removed from the 3 age decks. This is my one negative of the game. It can be disappointing to learn that you were planning on going for Science/Military victory and that option is not really available to you based on the cards randomly removed from the deck. Overall, this is decent 2-player game. There are other 2-player game I prefer.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
A very solid 2p game, with a minimal time investment and shallow learning curve. Multiple paths to victory add tension and strategic flexibility to the experience as well. Not only can you pursue military and science as a means of victory, but you can also leverage them to maneuver your opponent into weakened positions, forcing them to take sub-optimal moves, thereby acquiring and maintaining control of the game for yourself. The military track is a bit boring as it is just a push-of-war, but the technology cards are interesting. 7 different technology symbols win the game, but for each pair you manage to acquire you gain a very powerful progress token. Managing and choosing between these to science paths is very interesting. The game feels a bit over balanced, but it has been boiled down well for two players, and offers a bit of a deeper feel than most other 2p-exclusive titles.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Thematically similar to but mechanically very different from 7 Wonders, most notably in how "drafting" functions (although resources, military, science, and wonders themselves are also pretty far from the 7 Wonders implementation thereof). Cards are [partially] layered in alternative face-up and face-down rows. At first, only the foremost face-up cards can be "drafted", but as cards are [entirely] uncovered, they become available (and flipped face-up if face-down). Unlike the original game, this becomes a game of denial and risk management first and foremost. You must avoid making available a military or science card to an opponent who's strong in that area (both are insta-win conditions in Duel), but half the cards are hidden, so good luck with that. 

I can see how some people would enjoy the tension that arises from this ("no whammies"), and I understand that 7 Wonders has a similar lack of control in what cards intermediary players draft/pass, but this mechanic seems too luck-based in Duel. Perhaps with greater knowledge of all possible cards in an age, face-down cards become largely predictable, but I don't care for this kind of mechanic.

I'll try playing with all face-up cards a few times to see how that goes.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

A játék BGG helyezésével is tisztában vagyok. Sőt, Bruno Cathala sem ismeretlen számomra, megannyi játékáról olvastam jót – mindazonáltal még nem volt szerencsém egyik játékához sem –, tehát az előjelek roppant kedvezőek voltak. RATING: 9
A fantastic 2 player experience! The tension is high all the way to the end because of the two "sudden death"-criteria. The wonders create sudden change of "turn order" due to the extra turn actions, so you can never feel certain which card could be at your disposal next time. Each game feel very different, and there are certainly a lot of ways to win the game. Even money can be a strategy to win this game (unlike the original game).
I must say this game was a big surprise for me. I never would have imagined this to be a close to 10 for me.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
A very wonderful 2 player game that I enjoy with my non-gamer girlfriend.

Pros:
1. Many concepts(which add complexity), yet not complicated or hard to understand.
2. Quick to play
3. Gorgeous art that captures the eyes of even the non-gamers( My girlfriend would always say yes to a game of duel just because of the art.)
+ The cover is composed of a male and female, makes it feel like a couple game.
4. Game is not "strategic" , but it's tactical decisions can be very complex to make and game changing, adding to the fun and challenge.
5. It's fun to talk about your city after the game ends! ("Your city is so full of swords, armor, sweat, and steel that you don't even have the space for the bath").

Cons:
1. May feel stale if players prefer a more "strategic" game that feels like a more long term game.(It's just isn't what this game is about)
2. May feel unfair/boring once players decide that going for the other 2 victory conditions is impossible or considerably harder compared to going for the usual victory condition(Points victory).

RATING: 9
Since I had played 7 Wonders, picking up the modifications for this two player game was easy.  This game also includes some improvements, such as stand-out linking symbols instead of small hard to see building names.  I felt the handling of Science 
 is an improvement because it cuts out the scoring some newbies found confusing.  Also the Military attack is simplified, which I like because that was how I won my first game!  Card drafting demands planning ahead due to face-up/face-down cards.  I feel this is a more strategic game than 7 Wonders, because I have more control with 1 opponent rather than with maybe 4 with whom I have no direct contact.
     Wonder boards came severely warped, which was a disappointment although does not effect play.
     I prefer this game over 7 Wonders.

RATING: N/A

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I love this game, originally bought it as a solution to not having a stable enough group to play a full game of 7 Wonders but still wanting to be able to enjoy the experience once in a while.
Unfortunately it doesn't quite scratch that same itch, but it's an excellent game on its own, and I'd recommend it with or without the ties to 7 Wonders.
Being 2-player, it feels much more harshly competitive than the main game does, and this can lend to some interesting scenarios. For example: as in the base game you can choose to build, burn, or build a wonder with a card each turn. I've had a game where almost half of an entire age was burned by someone so dead-set on a military victory that was simply focused on keeping me from getting victory and military points.
Overall I'd gladly recommend this to anyone who loves the base game but has trouble finding time for everyone to get together and have a nice full game of it going, it won't fill up an evening as readily as the main game will but it'll provide a nice starter for a game night as it's lightweight and easy to set up and play.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.75
I'm not 100% sure if I like this more than its older... brother?
Nevertheless, I'm pretty sure I'm enjoying this as much as I'd like to enjoy any new board game in my collection (which is say a lot). As a two player game (as such this is designed for) and as some kind of "filler" (although I don't love that word) this game is fantastic.
I sincerely don't get why some reviewers say they don't feel the interaction here... What!? I mean, what do they mean!? The interaction in 7WD is its spine! Each and every move you make should be done in a way that interacts, negatively and directly, with your opponent's interest or, surely, I bet you're playing this the wrong way.

There's the Science path to victory... there's, also, the military way: you cannot forget the game is winnable by whichever of these methods, but, most important, you should never forget to deny your opponent the path to victory thru any of them!

There are the Wonders, there are the playing cards distributed in patterns showing some pieces of information, putting out of sight, at the same time, other pieces...

Brilliant design, great game experience for two players!

(Well, I guess I must admit I'm 99% sure I like this more than its older...)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
For what it is (a quick, 2-player filler game), it's remarkable.  Every decision has a cascading effect on what you and your opponent are capable of, and an effect on how you and your opponent view the situation.  The players can also not think about it so much and just play the game.  It's as light or heavy as the player's want it to be.

My wife, who is not a gamer, enjoyed it during our trial play.  I was able to setup, teach, and complete a game with her in under 30 minutes.  She said she'd liked it and would like to play it again.

I should also note this is a game I feel the need to sleeve the cards as they are flimsy and bowed.  I'm not a fan of sleeving, but I simply have to in this case.

RATING: 7
The Duel version is a conversion of the original 7 Wonders into a package better suitable for two players. Even though the central mechanism has been swapped out entirely there are enough similarities that those who already know its big brother will feel right at home. The  zero-sum nature of the two-player duel and the added instant win conditions add a bit of spice to the otherwise rather sedate proceedings. All in all, in does fairly well what it says on the tin.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
7 Wonders definitely scratches the 7 Wonders itch, but for two! It is quite different in the way the card drafting works, but the set collection is very much the same. There are enough differences to make this a very interesting game- specifically the card drafting "pyramid" mechanic. I'm not a big fan of alternate auto-win scenarios in point-based games (and Duel has two of them) but I can understand why they were introduced and as long as they are balanced then I think they are fine. More plays will get this figured out. Also, the luck of the draw can be killer every now and then. Of course, you can do your best to force your opponent to take a card so that you can take the card underneath, but sometimes the perfect card that is hidden is revealed and swings the game. But this is often feels like risk management rather than blind luck, so no real worries. The rulebook was also not great, leaving out some important details (like Guild rules) unless you read the card summaries at the end. And those points are poorly translated to boot! But finer sticky points aside, a very good game which I'm sure my impression will grow as I play!

RATING: 8
Sleeved
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
INITIAL IMPRESSION
Such a great 2p drafting game. I've always liked open (rochester) draft and this game does it in a very clever and thematic way.

The game really draws out the feeling of 7 wonders with the military, science, culture ways to win along with the wonders themselves. It's so fast and easy to play but offers a lot of replay-ability with how the cards come up, who goes for what and just the very tactical nature of the game is right up my alley.

I can't wait to get in more plays of this one.

MORE PLAYS:
Game continues to be solid but the variability in the cards is starting to get samey and there aren't as many tactical options at times. Expansion with more cards would be a welcomed addition but I'm not sure if that might unbalance the distribution between science/military/culture. Currently I feel science is too hard to go for

EXPANSION:
A must imo to help break up the deterministic card acquisition once extra turn wonders aren't available. This tactic extra option to do something while not removing a card from the pool is huge. The pantheon itself is avg but I do appreciate that it makes scientific victory more of a possibility (it's almost impossible in the base game against someone paying attention)

I like the guilds more than the Temples but I understand why they changed it (they could be more swingy)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Light euro card game - rework of the parent 7 Wonders game into a 2 player duel - get some resource cards and then build VP. Luck of the draw can be a significant factor in the first half of the game and can largely determine the winner. The game has a couple of alternate paths to victory so players need to be alert to how the resource engine is developing and try to react as early as possible. Getting the appropriate resource cards early means you have the best chance at any of the victory conditions of course but the game plays quickly so not a huge problem - reset and try again.

All the bits are very good.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I've not played the original 7 Wonders, so can't make a comparison between the two or comment on whether this makes up for the shortcomings of the original game's 2-player mode, but I was still excited to get to know Duel on its own terms. I can't help but admire how perfectly designed this game is. It really forces you to think on your toes and pull in lots of different directions. For example, even if you weren't planning on being militaristic, if your opponent *is* then you'll have to play at least a couple of military cards (or at least junk them to take them out of the game) to stop your opponent gaining a military victory. However, in spite of its technical brilliance, it's ended up being one of those games I really like but don't quite love. I think the main flaw for me is it doesn't quite immerse me in the theme. It still feels just a bit abstract. But for a short, simple game it's certainly entertaining and has great replayability value, so it's perfect as a quick "filler" Eurogame.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
Clearly people are enjoying this, but I just don't understand the appeal. The layout is much too constrained, and does not serve as a good substitute for drafting. Most turns will present exactly one obvious "choice." There just isn't any room to make interesting maneuvers or plans, and it's the random layout of the structure that decides your fate. Truly a scripted game with almost no player agency.

7 Wonders Duel also seems unnecessary, because the two-player version of the original 7 Wonders is outstanding! I think people see "neutral player" and think that it signals some kind of kludgy workaround. But the battle to manipulate the neutral city makes for a more layered, more skillful, and more exciting game (compared to a multi-handed game of 7 Wonders).

RATING: 9
7 Wonders Duel is awesome and has become a go-to 2-player game in my group. I love the tweaks to the 7 wonders system that have been made, from the "Rochester"-type drafting system (visible cards make the game MUCH easier to teach than classic 7 wonders) to the utility of military and science. In particular, I love that science can outright win the game, or at least get you useful technologies. It fits that "building a civilization" feel a little more.

Love 7 wonders: duel, and I am definitely looking forward to the Pantheon expansion!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Nice simple play but lots of depth, Different win conditions and age structures keep the replayability high. Really has some interesting lines of thought and forces you to be adaptable and switch gears partway through the game. Overall has a very nice flow to it, while still being quite deep.

There've been a lot of very close games of this, usually a Military or Science focus either barely getting there or barely missing and losing to a decisive civilian victory.

Pantheon breaks up the usually smooth flow with a very strategic staccato. The ability to not alter the pyramid is very interesting and opens up lots of additional tactical options. The god effects themselves are unique and interesting. An essential expansion, I'll play with it every time outside of teaching.

Have Pantheon

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Csodák háborúja
Kis fanyalgással kezdeném, mert ahogy bejelentették ennek a játéknak a hírét, azt gondoltam, milyen szuper lesz, ha az alapdobozhoz kiadnak egy olyan kiegészítőt, amelynek segítségével a régi kártyákat, csodákat használva 2 játékos is kellemesen szórakozhat (tudod, hogy az alapban is van két személyes játék, de azt nem szeretem – van ilyen). Na nem ez történt.
Az eddig megismert 7 Csoda világon alapulva újabb "pénztárcanyitogató" játék érkezett épp karácsony előtt időzítve (és biztosan tervben van már egy kieg is hozzá).
Aki az alapjátékot ismeri, pár perc alatt megismerkedhet a szabályokkal és indulhat is az első játék. Újoncoknak is könnyen emészthetőek ezen változat regulái, ikonrendszere. Maga a játék is barátságos kis dobozban foglal helyet, bár elsőre meglepő lesz a benne foglalt kártyák kis mérete annak, aki többször játszott már az előddel.
Újdonságként nem csak a játék végi pontozás alapján nyerhet valaki, hanem akár katonai fölényünkkel, akár tudományos ismereteink nagyságával „földbe döngölhetjük” játékostársunkat. A korábban már megismert pénzszerzés és nyersanyag vásárlás is változáson ment át. Csodafronton is eleve néggyel indul mindenki, amiből összesen 7 építhető meg, valamint a csodákban rejlő „újra te következel” képességgel is jól lehet taktikázni, annak ellenére, hogy a játéktéren elhelyezkedő lapformáció egyes kártyáit nem ismered.
Életképes, gyors, 7 Csoda utánérzés játék került ki alkotóik kezéből.
A játék előnyei mellett, azért van mint a „fekete levesbe” is aprítania, bár ezt mindenki másképpen értékelheti. A játékhoz elkészült csodák egyike-másika erősebb a többinél, ha szerencsés vagy és éppen 3-4 olyan csodát sikerül begyűjtened, amelyen szerepel az "újra te jössz” jutalom, annak megfelelő kihasználása esetében "garantált” a győzelem (persze, valakin ez sem segít). A korok kártyái között is találhatunk a többinél hasznosabb lapokat (pölö az első körben a 4 aranyas sárga lap, kombózva a raktáras sárga lapokkal a későbbi fordulók során egy-egy lap eldobásakor több aranyat hozva a „konyhára” rendkívüli előnyt jelentenek). Akinek ezzel nincs gondja, bízvást élvezi a játékot, plusz mivel a játék világsiker, így a kiadásra kerülő kiegészítőiben ezt már orvosolni lehet (más kérdés, hogy miért vegyek meg egy kiegészítőt a játék balanszolásához). A többieknek meg van más.
A játék mindenképpen jó, bár a BGG toplistán belüli előkelő helyezése "picit” túlértékelt. Annyira azért nem hagyott mély nyomot bennem. Magam az alapjátékot jobban szeretem.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.2
I shouldn't be surprised by this game but I am. It's way better than I thought it would be. This plays super quick and I LOVE the change introduce to military and science. I love the fact that a player can win the game before the end with Military supremacy or with Science domination. This adds an extra layer that you have to look up to what your opponent is doing to try to prevent him from achieving any of these victories while trying to do the same and gather enough victory point to win in the end if the game reaches its normal conclusion.

A Lot of great design decision which brings a game every has played and love and bring it even higher. I think I like Duel More than the original game because it's more tactical, less random and more personal.

RATING: 7
It starts out as a very interesting game but you may get disappointed when it ends. 
One of the goals (and maybe the most common one) is to amass the most victory points and I feel like they are not allocated where they should. It feels like the game is punishing you for making smart choices, such as building more Wonders, instead of just getting as many often free buildings as possible, for example. That makes it demotivating, in my opinion.
However, you can win with a military or scientific win instead, which makes the point system moot. The fact that there are different ways of winning makes it interesting so I still think that this game is a very nice game to play.

RATING: 8.5
An intriguing game about 7 wonders in a two-player battle.

The mechanics are different though. Now you will have 3 ways of winning instead of just counting victory points. Either win by collecting 6/7 different science symbol cards, win by total domination over your opponent in war points or win by traditionally having most VP at the end of the game!

Instead of drafting cards, players now select cards from a unique pyramid layed-out cards. Players in turn select a card to either play and own the resources, science cards or go up the war track or gain VP. Alternatively, players may complete wonders by tucking cards taken from the pyramid under their wonder to indicate that they completed them. Lastly, players can discard cards to collect money. Choose wisely as your action will affect your opponents stategy too!

I love this game. My best two player game :)
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.3
規則:
起始設定
起始7元，洗混科技圓片開五片，戰爭標誌放中間
每個時期抽掉三張卡，第三時期加入三張任意公會卡洗混
決定首家，首家翻開四張奇蹟卡挑一張，二家挑兩張，再輪到首家挑一張，再翻開四張卡，換二家挑一，首家挑二，最後一張給首家。
遊戲流程:
三個動作
a.	購買卡片: 卡片有需求須滿足，若有相關圖式建築物則無須花費，資源不夠花費為2元+對手擁有該資源數量(一個增加1元)=所需花費。(此資源不包刮奇蹟所提供)
b.	建設奇蹟: 覆蓋卡片於奇蹟底部，滿足奇蹟需求，資源不夠花費規則相同。奇蹟若有多一動則持續進行。
c.	棄牌: 拿取2元+本身擁有黃卡數量(一張1元)
## 若有兩個相同科技卡可以選取一片科技圓片 得到獎勵
## 武力增加推動武力軌超敵方前進，當超過某些區域會讓對手失去金錢
遊戲結束
1.	武力獲勝 抵達對方首都
2.	科技獲勝 收集到六種不同科技
3.	時期三結束比分數
咖啡色與灰色為基本資源卡
黃色為交易所，提供資源或金錢，以及購買資源優惠
綠色為科技卡 紅色為軍事卡
藍色為議院提供分數

奇蹟多一回合動作若是剛好時代結束則不可以執行

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.75
Probablemente el mejor juego de 2015, pero casi con total seguridad el mejor juego diseñado en exclusiva para dos jugadores. Desde luego, me parece muchísimo mejor que el original, al que tiene similitud sólo en el aspecto gráfico.

En lugar de un draft de cartas tradicional (toma 1 de un grupo de cartas y pasa el resto a tu compañero), las cartas se toman de un "mercado común" en forma de pirámide situado entre los dos jugadores en dónde algunas cartas no se pueden obtener por estar cubiertas por otras que, hasta que no son obtenidas por los participantes, no "liberan" las que tienen debajo. Por si fuera poco, la mitad de las cartas de la pirámide están ocultas, desvelándose a medida que los jugadores escogen las anteriores.

Además, hay condiciones de victoria alternativas a la de "gana el que más PV´s haya obtenido", por supremacía militar (una especie de "tira y afloja" en un tablerito aparte que ocasiona problemas al que va perdiendo y otorga PV´s al que gana cuando la partida acaba) y la supremacía científica (que la consigue el jugador cuyas cartas verdes muestren seis símbolos científicos distintos)

Me gusta que para tratarse de un juego tan sencillo, haya tantas estrategias distintas: bloqueo económico del contrincante, forzar al contrario a pagar cantidades ingentes de dinero por una estructura, generar dinero a través de estructuras de las cartas de comercio, forzarle a contrarrestar tu poder militar o algún hito científico...

PROS: Tiempo de preparación inicial adecuado, rápido de jugar, interactivo, estratégico y táctico. Cada forma de conseguir la victoria tiene su propio sistema (no son tres meros registros de PV´s)

CONS: Cartas demasiado pequeñas. Victoria por supremacía científica difícil de conseguir, así que se convierte más en una opción que debemos evitar al contrario más que en una opción que se pueda conseguir. El reglamento deja de lado las reglas de los gremios, que sólo leyendo el índice de cartas, te enteras de su funcionamiento. Tengo la sensación que las partidas se deciden con mucha frecuencia durante la era I cuando tienes un golpe de suerte y llega la carta de recursos que necesitas.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Very, very good! The general consensus is right. Muy buen juego para dos jugadores. Cada jugador debe construir un tableau (llamémosle ciudad) con cartas disponibles en una pirámide. Algunas cartas están visibles y disponibles, otras no. La selección es parte de la estrategia, porque cada jugador debe estar pendiente a lo que el oponente va formando y lo que busca. Hay que manejar recursos porque así se pagan las cartas que construyes en tu ciudad. Un mecanismo incorporado en los turnos te permite adquirir poder militar o cultural, que son formas de ganar el juego antes del final: supremacía militar o cultural. Juego genial, tenso y divertido que te mantiene concentrado hasta el último turno.

RATING: 4
I want to love this game but despite the great theme and production values the gameplay is badly broken. The drafting mechanic can favour one player with no recourse for the other, leading to a "railroaded" outcome from the first turn. It also allows arbitrary hostile player actions with no cost for being hostile. This can mean a player is left unable to compete for the second half of the game. Both the drafting (which is the crux of the whole game) and the sabotage ruin the fun of it.

Losing can be fun when you're outplayed, losing due to sabotage or run-away victories are definitely not fun, and yet I still want to love it. Most annoying!

RATING: 6
PRO: 
I enjoy the Duel aspect of the game. You feel in constant competition with your opponent. In larger games of 7 Wonders, that feeling wasn't as great. I felt I was mostly picking what is best for me, with some thought toward blocking other players from getting certain cards. Duel felt more focused, and you made more decisions based on the strategy and game play of your opponent. (I think this partly was due to the two non-victory-point win conditions that we added)

CON:
I still feel, as with the base game, that the randomness of the cards can in some situations outweigh a good strategy. For Example, sometimes the card you need, or that your opponent needs, is randomly opened up on your opponents turn, allowing them to take it rather than you. Obviously there is some manipulation of cards, but I still felt the level of randomness and chance of the layout of the cards, though not extremely distasteful, was not my favorite.

RATING: 6
A civilization building game (though on the abstract side), players take turns selecting cards to build their city in the hope of being able to construct wonders and earn points.  Victory also possible through science or military domination, it is a two-player only game that is streamlined into a sequence of choices that constantly force the player to weigh advantages and disadvantages.  Sometimes it's beneficial to trash a card that would help your opponent rather than take a card that would benefit your own city, and sometimes you have to accept the fact your opponent will get some advantage in order for you to get your own.  Some people complain the cards are small, but for me they fit the size of the game (and box).  Haven't played this game a huge amount, so still don't know how playable it is long-term.

RATING: 6
2015-12-27

Initial Rating: 6.0 (December 2015)

My desire to Play 7 Wonders: Duel was rather low. The reason was that, although I enjoyed 7 Wonders for a while in the past, I felt it was very repetitive so I ultimately sold my copy of the game and I feared this one will be the same. However I really enjoyed 7 Wonders: Duel, it has easy rules, it has a similar flavor than its parent game, it plays fast and it does offer (somewhat) interesting decisions (namely which card to buy but this decision can have far reaching consequences). If you have played 7 Wonders before, the explanation can be done under 5 minutes because they share many traits.

I LOVE that there are 3 ways to achieve victory, the usual VP approach, a  military victory or a scientific one so, even if one player is losing badly, he still have the chance to turn the tables and win the game. Also like the way the cards are arranged in each age. You can see some, some are hidden so you can plan a bit (a plsu) but also there is lots of uncontrollable luck (a dislike).

Bottom line, I liked Duel and I prefer it over 7 Wonders. I’m still not sure if I will buy it but it is certainly a possibility. I want to play it again soon to see if it can continue to hold my attention but perhaps it is too light for us right now. Its best feature is, by far, its short playtime.

Current Rating: 6.0
